# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy xDS v2 to v3 API Migration

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement both xDS v2 and v3 API handling: the versioned proto type conversion, the v2-to-v3 field renames (e.g., DiscoveryRequest), and the dual-version subscription handling in the ADS gRPC server.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

Perfect! I've completed my analysis of the Envoy repository and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

## Summary

I've identified **17 key C++ source files** in the envoyproxy/envoy v1.31.2 codebase that implement xDS v2/v3 API handling:

### Core Architecture
The implementation uses a sophisticated **template-based approach** with the unified xDS mux (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h`) that supports both:
- **State-of-the-World (SotW)** protocol via `GrpcMuxSotw`
- **Delta** protocol via `GrpcMuxDelta`

Both use v3 proto types (`envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest/Response` and their Delta variants).

### Key Components Identified

1. **xDS Mux Templates** - Uses RQ (Request) and RS (Response) template parameters for protocol flexibility
2. **Subscription State Management** - `BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ>` template with Delta and SotW implementations  
3. **Versioning Annotations** - Proto files mark v3 messages with `udpa.annotations.versioning.previous_message_type` pointing to v2 equivalents
4. **ADS Server Integration** - Factory pattern in `grpc_subscription_factory.cc` creates subscription adapters
5. **Type URL Routing** - `type_to_endpoint.cc` maps different xDS API types (CDS, EDS, LDS, RDS, etc.)

The dual-protocol architecture enables flexible protocol handling while maintaining backward compatibility through protobuf migration annotations.

At the core is the unified xDS mux implementation in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h, which uses template parameters (RQ for request type, RS for response type) to support different protocol versions. The template is instantiated twice: GrpcMuxSotw (State-of-the-World) using envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest/Response, and GrpcMuxDelta using envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response.\\n\\nThe subscription state management is abstracted through BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ> template in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h, which handles the protocol state for individual xDS subscriptions. Two concrete implementations are provided: DeltaSubscriptionState (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc) for delta xDS protocol and SotwSubscriptionState (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc) for state-of-the-world protocol. Both handle the getNextRequestInternal() and handleGoodResponse() methods that construct v3 proto messages.\\n\\nThe v2-to-v3 field renaming and versioning is handled through protobuf annotations. The api/envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.proto file contains DiscoveryRequest, DiscoveryResponse, DeltaDiscoveryRequest, and DeltaDiscoveryResponse messages, each marked with udpa.annotations.versioning.previous_message_type pointing to their v2 counterparts (e.g., \\\"envoy.api.v2.DiscoveryRequest\\\"). This annotation system maintains backward compatibility through the protobuf migration infrastructure.\\n\\nThe ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server subscription handling integrates these components through the grpc_subscription_factory.cc file, specifically the AdsConfigSubscriptionFactory::create() method, which creates GrpcSubscriptionImpl instances that wrap the GrpcMux objects. The factory pattern in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_factory.cc allows runtime selection between the legacy GrpcMuxImpl (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) and the unified XdsMux::GrpcMuxSotw/GrpcMuxDelta implementations based on feature flags (envoy.reloadable_features.unified_mux).\\n\\nType URL-based routing for different xDS APIs (CDS, EDS, LDS, RDS, etc.) is handled in source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.cc, which maintains mappings for v3 service endpoints including RouteDiscoveryService, ClusterDiscoveryService, EndpointDiscoveryService, ListenerDiscoveryService, and others. The type_url field in DiscoveryRequest/Response messages is used by the ADS server to multiplex multiple resource types over a single gRPC stream.\\n\\nThe dual-protocol architecture is achieved through the generic GrpcStream<RQ, RS> interface in the gRPC mux implementation, which allows the same subscription and stream management logic to handle both request and response message types transparently. Error handling and NACK/ACK mechanisms are implemented in subscription_state.h through the handleResponse() and handleBadResponse() methods that set error_detail fields in the request messages.\"\n}\n",

subscription system. At the core is the unified xDS mux implementation in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h, which uses template parameters (RQ for request type, RS for response type) to support different protocol versions. The template is instantiated twice: GrpcMuxSotw (State-of-the-World) using envoy::service::discovery::v3::DiscoveryRequest/Response, and GrpcMuxDelta using envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest/Response.\\n\\nThe subscription state management is abstracted through BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ> template in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h, which handles the protocol state for individual xDS subscriptions. Two concrete implementations are provided: DeltaSubscriptionState (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/delta_subscription_state.h/cc) for delta xDS protocol and SotwSubscriptionState (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/sotw_subscription_state.h/cc) for state-of-the-world protocol. Both handle the getNextRequestInternal() and handleGoodResponse() methods that construct v3 proto messages.\\n\\nThe v2-to-v3 field renaming and versioning is handled through protobuf annotations. The api/envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.proto file contains DiscoveryRequest, DiscoveryResponse, DeltaDiscoveryRequest, and DeltaDiscoveryResponse messages, each marked with udpa.annotations.versioning.previous_message_type pointing to their v2 counterparts (e.g., \\\"envoy.api.v2.DiscoveryRequest\\\"). This annotation system maintains backward compatibility through the protobuf migration infrastructure.\\n\\nThe ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server subscription handling integrates these components through the grpc_subscription_factory.cc file, specifically the AdsConfigSubscriptionFactory::create() method, which creates GrpcSubscriptionImpl instances that wrap the GrpcMux objects. The factory pattern in source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_factory.cc allows runtime selection between the legacy GrpcMuxImpl (source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc) and the unified XdsMux::GrpcMuxSotw/GrpcMuxDelta implementations based on feature flags (envoy.reloadable_features.unified_mux).\\n\\nType URL-based routing for different xDS APIs (CDS, EDS, LDS, RDS, etc.) is handled in source/common/config/type_to_endpoint.cc, which maintains mappings for v3 service endpoints including RouteDiscoveryService, ClusterDiscoveryService, EndpointDiscoveryService, ListenerDiscoveryService, and others. The type_url field in DiscoveryRequest/Response messages is used by the ADS server to multiplex multiple resource types over a single gRPC stream.\\n\\nThe dual-protocol architecture is achieved through the generic GrpcStream<RQ, RS> interface in the gRPC mux implementation, which allows the same subscription and stream management logic to handle both request and response message types transparently. Error handling and NACK/ACK mechanisms are implemented in subscription_state.h through the handleResponse() and handleBadResponse() methods that set error_detail fields in the request messages.\"\n}\n",
